 Fig. 22  Chemical structures of the copolymers p4.81–p4.84. 
 Fig. 23  Chemical structures of copolymers containing triarylamine units. 
Poly(3-hexylthiophene) (P3HT) is one of the most common hole conductors investigated for bulk heterojunction solar cells171 and p-channel FETs.172 The first environmentally stable and soluble poly(3-alkylthiophenes) (P3ATs) were synthesized by Elsenbaumer173 in 1985, using a method similar to that used to prepare 2,5-polythiophene. Polymerization reactions of asymmetric 3-hexylthiophene (3HT) may result in three different coupling sites along the polymer chain, i.e. 2,5′-(head-to-tail, HT), 2,2′-(head-to-head, HH) and 5,5′-(tail-to-tail, TT) (Scheme 5). Therefore, synthetic methodologies have been developed to control P3HT regiochemistry, which greatly affects several structural, electronic and optical properties of this polymer family.171,174
 Scheme 5  Poly(3-hexylthiophene) regioisomers. 
Particularly, a structural regioregular head-to-tail (HT) arrangement is greatly desirable, since polymers of this type of regioregularity exhibit very interesting physicochemical properties, which facilitate their application in organic electronics. Regioregular HT-P3HT macromolecules can preorganize via a three-dimensional self assembly, resulting in efficient two-dimensional hole transport71 with high mobilities and current density.172b,175–177 Self-organization in P3HT results in a lamellar structure with two-dimensional conjugated sheets formed by interchain stacking. Sirringhaus et al.71 suggested that the π–π stacked crystalline planes can adopt two different orientations (i.e. parallel and normal to the film) depending on the P3HT regioregularity, processing conditions and the type of the substrate.
In essentially all applications of P3HT in organic electronics, regioregularity turned out to be one of the key parameters. Its decrease from 96% to 70% results in a drop in the hole mobility by three orders of magnitude. Regioregularity affects the charge transport not only in the semiconducting, undoped form of P3HT but also in the electrochemically doped polymer, as demonstrated by Jiang et al.176 who reported worsening of the electrical transport parameters in thin films of doped P3HT with decreasing degree of regioregularity. These findings were ascribed to the better supramolecular organization and higher extent of π-stacking in regioregular P3HT, as concluded from electrochemical, EPR, UV-vis-NIR, and X-ray diffraction measurements.
The aspect of regioregularity in P3HT also plays an important role in its band gap control. The random polymerization of 3-hexylthiophene leads to a large degree of HH coupling that decreases the effective conjugation in the chain and blue-shifts the absorption maxima, due to a large twist-distortion.174,178
Besides the HT regioregularity, molecular mass and its polydispersity are also important parameters to control electronic, spectroscopic and electrochemical properties of P3HT. The first study of the effect of Mn on spectroscopic and electrochemical properties of regioregular P3HT was undertaken by Trznadel et al.179 who investigated five fractions of this polymers of reduced PDI. They found that the conjugation length in P3HT increases with Mn whereas the IP value decreases.
Sirringhaus et al.71 reported that the molecular mass has a considerable impact on the crystalline connectivity and ordering of pristine P3HT spin-cast films, thus influencing the charge carrier mobility of the polymer. Kline et al.72a,b,180 observed that varying the molecular mass of P3HT by one order of magnitude results in a four order of magnitude change in the hole mobility. The low mobility, low molecular-mass films revealed a highly ordered structure consisting of nanorods, whereas the high-molecular mass films, showing an increased μh had an isotropic nodule structure. The best mobilities were obtained for relatively high molecular mass P3HT (Mn > 25 kDa by Size Exclusion Chromatography (SEC), using PS standards) under slow evaporating conditions on hydrophopic substrates.181 Verilhac et al.73 found that this increase of μh persists at Mn = 120 kDa (SEC), PS standards. Zen et al.172a,182 reported on the optical, structural and electrical characterization of thin films prepared from different molecular mass fractions of regioregular P3HT. They demonstrated that lowering the molecular mass of P3HTs dramatically decreases the field-effect mobility and this was mainly ascribed to the ability of high-molecular mass fractions to adopt a planar backbone conformation which allows a close interchain contact. To support this hypothesis the authors correlated the well known thermochromic effect of regioregular P3HT183 with the charge carrier mobility. The thermochromic effect is manifested by a hypsochromic shift of the π–π* transition band in the UV-vis spectrum of a solid P3HT layer with increasing temperature. This shift is associated with a temperature-induced increase of the torsion angle between the adjacent thiophene rings in the polymer chain. The authors correlated the increasing spectral hypsochromic shift with decreasing charge carrier mobility, demonstrating in this manner that a more twisted conformation hindered the transport of charge carriers.
P3HT can be obtained via nickel-catalyzed coupling polymerization, palladium-catalyzed coupling polymerization (Stille coupling and Suzuki–Miyaura coupling), direct arylation polymerization and oxidative (chemical or electrochemical) coupling polymerization (Table 2).

The first synthesis of regioregular HT-P3HT was reported by McCullough's group in 1992.74,184 The regioregular polymerization of 3-hexylthiophene can be controlled by selective lithiation of 2-bromo-3-alkylthiophene with lithium diisopropylamine followed by transmetalation using magnesium bromide to yield the organomagnesium intermediate. The use of a Ni(dppp)Cl2 catalyst for the polymerization of this intermediate gives the corresponding P3HT with 98% head-to-tail regioselectivity (Table 2, entry 1). The second method to obtain highly regioselective P3HT (Table 2, entry 2) was subsequently developed by Chen and Rieke.185 Highly reactive zinc (known as “Rieke zinc”) undergoes a selective oxidative addition to 2,5-bromo-3-hexylthiophene to yield the 2-(bromozinco)-3-hexyl-5-bromothiophene intermediate in quantitative yields. This intermediate undergoes then regiospecific polycondensation to yield HT P3HT.
Later, McCullough's group186a,d reported another method for the synthesis of regioregular P3HT by Grignard metathesis (GRIM)186 (Table 2, entry 3). Treatment of 2,5-dibromo-3-hexylthiophene with a variety of alkyl Grignard reagents resulted in two metalated regioisomers via a magnesium exchange reaction. Introduction of a catalytic amount of Ni(dppp)Cl2 into this isomeric mixture afforded P3HT of regioregularity >99%. McCullough186d and Yokozawa40,41 independently demonstrated that the Grignard metathesis polymerization of 3-hexylthiophene proceeds by the living chain growth mechanism instead of the traditionally accepted step growth polycondensation. The molecular mass of the resulting polymer can be controlled by the monomer to the Ni catalyst feed ratio and the polydispersity of the resulting polymer is low (PDI from 1.2 to 1.4)40,186d,187 (Table 2, entry 4). Taking into account that the described reaction can be carried out at RT on a relatively large scale, the Grignard metathesis (GRIM)–Kumada catalyst transfer polycondensation (KCTP) has become the most widely used method for producing P3HT with predetermined high molecular mass.
Another group of methods employed for the synthesis of regioregular P3HT include palladium-catalyzed cross-coupling reactions. Iraqi and Barker188 have investigated the synthesis of regioregular P3HT through the Stille reaction, using 3-hexyl-2-iodo-5-(tributylstannyl)thiophene (Scheme 6). The polymerization reactions were carried out in different solvents at reflux temperature, and in the presence of Pd(PPh3)4 (3 mol%) as a catalyst. Molecular masses of regioregular P3HT prepared by this method were Mn = 10–16 kDa (SEC, PS standards) with PDI = 1.2–1.4 (Table 2, entry 5).
 Scheme 6  Synthesis of regioregular P3HT by Stille coupling reactions. 
Liversedge et al.189 investigated a range of Pd catalysts with bulky, electron-rich phosphane ligands for the synthesis of regioregular P3HT by the Suzuki reaction (Table 2, entry 6). Such complexes were previously found190 to be too active for a range of cross-coupling reactions, including Suzuki couplings. Indeed, although Suzuki coupling was used to prepare oligothiophenes191 polymerizations were found to be more difficult to be carried out successfully. In the use of thiophene boronates, deboronation turned out to be a problem, representing the termination of polymerization by aryl group transfer from the PPh3 ligand employed.192 Li et al.193 reported a novel efficient zero valent catalyst precursor, tris[tri(2-thienyl)phosphine]palladium (Pd(PTh3)3), and demonstrated that this catalyst was superior to Pd(PPh3)4 typically used in Suzuki–Miyaura coupling polymerization of thiophene-based substrates. 3-Hexyl-5-iodothiophene-2-boronic pinacol ester was used as a monomer in this polymerization (Scheme 7). The HT regioregularity of this P3HT was over 97%. The authors also found that the use of this new catalyst leads to a higher reaction yield and a higher molecular mass (compare entries 7 and 8 in Table 2).
 Scheme 7  Synthesis of regioregular P3HT by Suzuki–Miyaura coupling reactions. 
The palladium-catalyzed C–H activation was used for efficient coupling of numerous aromatic molecules via direct arylation. Wang et al.66 applied this strategy to the synthesis of regioregular P3HT (Table 2, entry 9), successfully polymerizing 2-bromo-3-hexylthiophene using Herrmann's catalyst and tris(2-dimethylaminophenyl)phosphine as catalyst precursors. P3HT was obtained with high molecular mass (Mn = 30600) and high regioregularity (98%) in quantitative yields (99%).
More recently Wang et al.67 have described the synthesis of regioregular P3HT end-capped with p-substituted phenyl groups via direct arylation (Table 2, entry 10).
In the past century Amou et al.35 performed a detailed study with the goal to establish optimum conditions for oxidative polymerization of 3HT with FeCl3 as an oxidant in chloroform. The best head-to-tail content of 89% was obtained for polymerizations carried out at −45 °C for 72 h with the initial monomer concentration of 0.02 mol L−1 (Table 2 entry 11). Yu et al.194 reported the oxidative coupling polymerization of 3-hexylthiophene with O2/VO(acac)2/FeCl3 as a catalyst. By lowering the polymerization temperature to −20 °C an increased head-to-tail content of 81% was observed, but correspondingly the yield decreased to 18% (Table 2, entry 12).
Regioregular poly(alkylthiophenes) of HH–TT regioregularity were obtained either from 4,4′-dialkyl-2,2′-bithiophenes195 or from 3,3′-dialkyl-2,2′-bithiophenes196 by chemical or electrochemical oxidative polymerization. HH–TT poly(alkylthiophenes) show higher optical band gap than the corresponding HT poly(alkylthiophenes) which can be ascribed to higher chain torsion angle, induced by the HH couplings. HH–TT poly(alkylthiophenes) do not show the field effect in the p-channel FET configuration. Contrary to HT poly(alkylthiophenes) they show strong photo- and electroluminescence.197
Poly(3,3′′-dialkyl-2,2′:5′,2′′-terthiophene)s (p4.1) were first reported by Gallazzi et al.198 The monomer was synthesized by coupling 3-alkyl-2-iodothiophene in the form of a Grignard reagent with 2,5-diiodothiophene in the presence of the Ni(dppp)Cl2 catalyst. However, presently this monomer is usually synthesized from 2-bromo-3-alkyl thiophene and the diboroderivative of thiophene through Suzuki coupling because in this case the purification process is simpler. It can then be oxidatively polymerized to give the corresponding polymer.199 Alternatively, poly(3,3′′-dioctyl-2,2′:5′,2′′-terthiophene)s (p4.1) can also be obtained by Stille-type polycondensation of 5,5′-dibromo-4,4′-dioctyl-2,2′:5′,2′′-bithiophene with distannylated thiophene.200p4.1 can be used for the fabrication of p-channel FETs. Similarly as in the case of regioregular P3HT, the FET mobility of its charge carriers is strongly Mn dependent.72c
Poly(3,3′′-dialkylquaterthiophene)s i.e. solution processable poly(thiophene) derivatives containing one alkyl group per two thiophene rings were prepared by oxidative polymerization of the corresponding monomer and tested as components of OFETs.201 OFET active layers were fabricated from structurally ordered nanoparticles of poly(3′,3′′-didodecylquaterthiophene)s, p4.2, yielding transistors of very high performance (Table 3).

A series of selenophene-based copolymers, poly(5,5′-bis(3-dodecylthiophene-2-yl)-2,2′-biselenophene), p4.3, and poly(5,5′-bis(4,4′-didodecyl-2,2′-bithiophen-5-yl)-2,2′-biselenophene), p4.4, were synthesized by Stille and oxidative coupling reactions.202 The FET characteristics of these polymers were strongly dependent on the intermolecular ordering of the polymer chains. p4.3 exhibited a reasonable hole transporting mobility of 0.02 cm2 V−1 s−1 due to its excellent intermolecular ordering, whereas p4.4 exhibited a very poor mobility of 1.4 × 10−5 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3) due to its amorphous nature, which resulted from the polymer chain torsion induced by the head to head coupled decylthiophenes. The thin film of a blend of p4.3 and PCBM (phenyl C61 butyric acid methyl ester) was used as a bulk heterojunction layer in photovoltaic cells. The PCE (power conversion efficiency) of a cell composed of a blend of p4.3 and PCBM (1:4, w/w) reached 1.4% under A.M. 1.5 G illumination, 100 mW cm−2. This PCE was higher than those achievable using p4.2:PCBM system.203
A regioregular copolymer of 2,2′-bithiophene and didodecyl 2,2′-bithiophene-4,4′-dicarboxylate was prepared by Stille coupling (p4.5). This macromolecular compound containing withdrawing ester groups can be considered as a donor–acceptor polymer with unsubstituted bithiophene groups as the donating units.204
Polythiophene derivatives containing fused thiophene rings constitute an interesting class of organic semiconductors. Poly(2,5-bis(3-alkylthiophene-2-yl)thieno[3,2-b]thiophenes) containing no substituents on the thieno[3,2-b]thiophene unit but two long tetradecyl chains (R = C14H29, p4.6) (and R = C12H25, p4.7, R = C10H21, p4.8) on the bithiophene unit were reported by McCulloch et al.205 Those polymers were prepared by a Stille condensation of 2,5-bis(trimethylstannyl)thieno[3,2-b]thiophene and the appropriate 5,5′-dibromo-4,4′-dialkyl-[2,2′]bithiophene in analogy to a previously reported procedure (Scheme 8).206 The Michael addition of ethylmercaptoacetate to the 3-position of 3-bromothiophene-2-carboxaldehyde followed by elimination of bromide and an aldol condensation yielded ethyl thieno[3,2-b]thiophene-2-carboxylate. This intermediate product was then hydrolyzed to the corresponding carboxylic acid. Decarboxylation by copper and quinoline led to the formation of thieno[3,2-b]thiophene. Lithiation of thieno[3,2-b]thiophene and quenching with trimethyltin chloride afforded 2,5-bis-trimethylstannylthieno[3,2-b]thiophene (Scheme 8).207 The TT arrangement of the alkyl chains on the bithiophene units also minimizes the steric interactions between neighboring units, leading to coplanarity of the backbone and hence promoting self-organization. It was found that the hairy rigid-rods p4.6 (p4.7 and p4.8) exhibit a liquid-crystalline behaviour and self-assemble into a highly crystalline domain with lamellar and π-stacked polymer chains.208 The side chain attachment density in p4.6 (p4.7 and p4.8) is sufficiently low to allow interdigitation, which provides a three-dimensional ordering.209 Due to this enhanced structural order, a remarkably high field-effect hole mobility of 0.3–1.0 cm2 V−1 s−1 was obtained (Table 3).205,210 This value is even higher than that reported for regioregular P3HT (0.1–0.2 cm2 V−1 s−1).205 Films of p4.6 deposited by simple spin-casting showed remarkably ordered in-plane microstructure originating from the liquid-crystallinity of this polymer which facilitated the transport of carriers between the electrodes.211
 Scheme 8  Synthetic route to pepare p4.6, p4.7 and p4.8. 
The synthesis of poly(2,5-bis(2-thienyl)-3,6-dipentadecylthieno[3,2-b]thiophene) (p4.9) containing substituents on the thieno[3,2-b]thiophene unit is depicted in Scheme 9.212 Stille coupling of 2,5-dibromo-3,6-dipentadecylthieno[3,2-b]thiophene with 2-tributylstannylthiophene, followed by bromination, gave 2,5-bis(2-bromothienyl)-3,6-dipentadecylthieno[3,2-b]thiophene.213 Subsequent Yamamoto dehalogenative coupling polymerization was carried out in the presence of a slight excess of Ni(COD)2 (COD: 1,5-cyclooctadiene) and catalytic amounts of 2,2′-dipyridyl in refluxing toluene.212 The FETs properties of p4.9 were tested using a bottom-gate, top-contact TFT device configuration built on an n-doped silicon wafer. Before annealing, the device showed a saturated FET mobility of ca. 0.08 cm2 V−1 s−1 and a current on/off ratio of 106. This mobility increased to about 0.25 cm2 V−1 s−1 after annealing of the active layer at ca. 150 °C (Table 3).212
 Scheme 9  Synthetic route to prepare p4.9. 
Poly(2,5-bis(3′-dodecyl-2,2′-bithiophen-5-yl)-3,6-dimethylthieno[3,2-b]thiophene) (p4.10) and poly(5′,5′′-(3,6-dimethylselenopheno[3,2-b]selenophene-2,5-diyl)bis(3-dodecyl-2,2′-bithiophene)) (p4.11) containing two fused aromatic rings either 3,6-dimethylthieno[3,2-b]thiophene or 3,6-dimethylselenopheno[3,2-b]selenophene as central units were synthesized via oxidative coupling reactions.214 An important advantage of this synthetic pathway is the possibility to obtain the fused bithiophene segment in a one step reaction (Scheme 10).215 Both polymers were prepared by oxidative polymerization with FeCl3 in chlorobenzene. FETs prepared from p4.10 and p4.11 by solution processing exhibited a charge carrier mobility of 0.03–0.04 cm2 V−1 s−1, with a high on/off ratio of 106 (Table 3).214
 Scheme 10  Synthetic pathway leading to p4.10 and p4.11. 

p4.10 and p4.11 contain an unsubstituted thiophene spacer between the alkyl substituted thiophene ring and the alkyl substituted thieno[3,2-b]thiophene unit (or its selenophene analogue). The presence of this spacer turned out to be crucial for the highly ordered supramolecular organization and electronic properties of these polymers since it diminishes the distortion of the core units caused by the repulsion of the methyl chains attached to the fused aromatic ring and enables interdigitation of the dodecyl substituents in neighbouring macromolecules. Lack of this spacer leads to polymers of higher chain torsion, less ordered structural organization and poor FET mobility as measured for poly(2,5-bis(3-dodecylthiophen-2-yl)-3,6-dimethylthieno[3,2-b]thiophene), p4.12, and poly(2,2′-(3,6-dimethylselenopheno[3,2-b]selenophene-2,5-diyl)bis(3-dodecylthiophene)), p4.13.214
A series of copolymers consisting of alternating β-alkylsubstituted fused thiophene and bithiophene segments (p4.14, p4.15 and p4.16) were successfully synthesized by He and Zhang.216 For these copolymers the π–π* transition band in the UV-vis spectra is blue shifted as compared to the corresponding band in the copolymers with unsubstituted fused thiophene units. This indicates that their IP is higher and they should be more stable with regard to oxidation.217 Recently, Youn et al. have reported218 a convenient “one-pot” [1 + 1 + 2] and [2 + 1 + 1] synthesis of tetrathienoacene – a building block used for the preparation of these polymers. Compared to the previous synthetic routes, this one-pot synthesis offers a more efficient way to obtain the condensed quaterthiophene-based reagent at low cost.
The hole mobility in thin layers of poly(2,5-bis(thiophene-2-yl)-(3,7-ditri-decanyltetrathienoacene), p4.15A, derived from the FET transfer characteristics, is 0.33 cm2 V−1 s−1, with an on/off ratio exceeding 105, and a threshold voltage of −10 V (Table 3).219
Three polymers, poly(2,5-bis(thiophene-2-yl)-(3,5-didecanyltrithienoacene)) (p4.14) poly(2,5-bis(thiophene-2-yl)-(3,7-didecanyltetrathienoacene)) (p4.15B), and poly(2,5-bis(thiophene-2-yl)-(3,6-didecanylpentathienoacene)) (p4.16) were synthesized by Stille polymerization.220 Polymers having the same alkyl substituent were chosen for a more accurate and meaningful comparison. OFET properties of these polymers were evaluated from the characteristics of specially fabricated test transistors (top contact, bottom gate, SiO2 dielectric). The measured mobilities strongly depended on the substrate surface treatment. The devices fabricated by spin-casting on the surface of SiO2 treated with octyltrichlorosilane (C8OTS) or hexamethyldisilazane (HMDS) exhibited one order magnitude higher mobility, two or three orders of magnitude higher on/off ratio, and much lower threshold voltage than the devices on bare substrates (Table 3). This indicates that alkylsilane self-assembled monolayers on the oxide surface can be used to decrease the oxygen contamination of the polymer film, decrease the trap sites, and improve the molecular chain packing order of the semiconductor layer on the dielectric/semiconductor interface, at least in the case of this family of polymers. No liquid crystallinity is observed for p4.14, p4.15 and p4.16 as judged from the DSC scans. A GIWAXS study confirmed that p4.15B can form tighter lamellae packing structures due to the proper arrangement of the substituents. On the other hand p4.14 and p4.16 macromolecules are packed much more loosely. AFM images are consistent with X-ray scattering results. The p4.15B polymer demonstrated the largest terrace structure among all three polymers, not surprisingly yielding the best device performance.220

p4.17 containing no substituents in the trithienoacene units but with two dodecyl chains on the bithiophene unit was prepared by Stille coupling polymerization of 2,6-bis-trimethyl-stannanyl-dithieno[3,2-b;2′,3′-d]thiophene with 5,5′-dibromo-4,4′-didocyl-[2,2′]bithiophene.221 It shows a FET mobility as high as 0.3 cm2 V−1 s−1 with a very high current on/off ratio of over 107 (Table 3). Moreover, p4.17 can also be processed in environmentally friendly hydrocarbon solvents such as hexane and heptane, and devices fabricated using these solvents still retain high FET performance characteristics.221
A series of semiconducting copolymers consisting of thiophene-dialkyl-trithienoacene and alkyl-bithiophene units (p4.18A–D) were synthesized by Lu et al.222 The energy gaps of these four copolymers are 2.4–2.5 eV, about 0.4 higher than that of regioregular of poly(3-hexylthiophene),223 which helps to decrease their sensitivity to ambient light and inhibits photoinduced excitation.224 The hole mobility, measured in the FET configuration, for films annealed at 180 °C was ca. 0.03 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3). It should be noted that all fabricated devices exhibited high environmental stability against oxygen contamination and against high ambient humidity (30%).
Thieno[2,3-b]thiophene, which is used as a building block in the synthesis of p4.19, is a stable aromatic heterocycle readily synthesized.225 Otsubo et al.225b reported its synthesis by the lithiation of 1-trimethylsilylpentadiyne with n-BuLi/t-BuOK, followed by trapping of the resultant anion with carbon disulfide. Subsequent ring closure afforded 2-trimethylsilylthieno[2,3-b]thiophene, which could readily be desilylated by treatment with tetrabutylammonium fluoride to yield thieno[2,3-b]thiophene.225c
Its copolymers with 4,4′-dialkyl 2,2′-bithiophenes, p4.19A and p4.19B, were prepared by Stille coupling.226 The thieno[2,3-b]thiophene unit prevents a fully conjugated pathway between the substituents at the 2 and 5 positions.227 As a result these polymers exhibit a somewhat higher IP (5.3 eV) than fully conjugated, planar thiophene polymers.
As already stated in Section 2.4 in conjugated polymers long alkyl substituents promote self-organization in the solid state. Moreover, in the case of p4.19A and p4.19B decyl and longer substituents are necessary to ensure their good solubility for printing using environmentally friendly solvents. Spin-coated p4.19A showed a lamellar structure with an interlayer spacing of 1.7 nm and a π-stacking distance of 0.37 nm, as evidenced by X-ray diffraction.226 FETs with p4.19A and p4.19B as active layers exhibited a good μh of 0.15 cm2 V−1 s−1 and 0.12 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.19A and p4.19B, respectively, under ambient conditions.226
Among polymers containing condensed thiophene rings, poly(thieno[3,4-b]thiophene) derivatives constitute an interesting case.228 The monomers thieno[3,4-b]thiophene derivatives can be readily electropolymerized through oxidative coupling at 2 and 5 positions. The resulting polymers show a very low band gap <1 eV – one of the lowest ever reported.
Thienylenevinylene derivatives consisting of a central vinylene group to which two alkylbithiophenes are attached are known to have an extended conjugated system.229 It is caused by the fact that the incorporation of a vinylene unit in an linear aromatic system reduces steric hindrance on successive aromatic rings.230 These monomers are very good building blocks for the corresponding polymers. Poly(1,2-(E)-bis[3-dodecylthiophene-2,2′-bithiophene-5-yl]ethene), p4.20, was prepared from the dibrominated monomer using Yamamoto coupling.231 Layers of this polymer, after annealing, showed an ordered supramolecular organization of lamellar-type with the dominant X-ray reflection corresponding to d = 1.44 nm. A rather low value of this distance, ascribed to the separation of π-stacked columns of conjugated macromolecules by side alkyl groups, seems to indicate a high degree of interdigitation of the dodecyl groups. IP of p4.20 (5.2 eV) is slightly higher than that of regioregular P3HT, suggesting its better air operating stability. FETs based on p4.20 showed a high charge carrier mobility of 0.15 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3).231 Exhibiting a high hole mobility and a low band-gap (1.85 eV) as well as an appropriate IP value, p4.20 can be considered as a donor in polymer bulk heterojunction (BHJ) photovoltaic cells. Such cells comprising p4.20 and [6,6]-phenyl-C71-butyric acid methyl ester (PC[71]BM) as an electron acceptor were fabricated. In preliminary tests, under nonoptimized conditions they showed a power-conversion efficiency (PCE) of 1.2%.231
Several polymeric semiconductors, containing other than thienoacene-type fused aromatic rings, have been synthesized and tested in recent years. Benzo[1,2-b:4,5-b′]dithiophene (BDT) constitutes an interesting building block for the design of such polymers. In discussing the synthesis of polymers containing the BDT unit it is instructive to present the concepts of benzannulation and thienannulation as two distinctly different synthetic approaches to this molecule or its derivatives (Scheme 11).232 In the benzannulation approach, the central benzene ring of BDT is constructed from two differently substituted thiophene derivatives via a set of thermodynamically driven condensation/aromatization reactions leading to the benzene ring formation.233 There are several drawbacks of these reactions, described in detail in ref. 232. In contrast, the synthesis of BDT through thienannulation starts from a readily available benzene derivative, and yields the desired product in a one pot procedure.234
 Scheme 11  Two approaches – benzannulation and thienannulation – to benzo[1,2-b:4,5-b′]dithiophene (BDT) derivatives. 

p4.21, an alternating copolymer of BDT and dialkylbithiophene, was obtained by oxidative polymerization of 4,8-dihexyl-2,6-bis(3-hexylthiophen-2-yl)benzo[1,2-b:4,5-b′]dithiophene. The monomer was prepared, in turn, by Suzuki coupling of 2,6-dibromo-4,8-dihexylbenzo[1,2-b:4,5-b′]dithiophene and 3-hexylthiophene-2-boronic acid pinacol ester.235 Thin films of p4.21 showed a highly ordered supramolecular organization with a π-stacking distance of 0.39 nm and a distance between the π-stacked columns of 1.61 nm, as revealed by grazing incidence X-ray diffraction (GIXRD) investigations. Its IP is by 0.22 eV higher than that of regioregular P3HT, making this polymer more resistant towards irreversible oxidation under air operating conditions. μh values extracted from the FET characteristics reached 0.15–0.25 cm2 V−1 s−1 with a current on/off ratio of 105–106 (Table 3). Only a slight decrease of the mobility was observed over a period of 30 days.235

p4.22 containing benzo[2,1-b:3,4-b′]dithiophene units, having two dodecyl chains attached to the central benzene ring, was prepared by oxidative polymerization with FeCl3.236 The presence of these alkyl substituents was necessary to induce the polymer solubility. Consisting of a sequence of fused aromatic rings the macromolecules of p4.22 lack sufficient flexibility for the formation of a highly ordered supramolecular organization in thin solid films. Moreover the distance between the macromolecules in a π-stacked column is unusually large (0.43 nm), significantly larger than in semiconductors showing high charge carrier mobilities.237 Indeed, p4.22 showed a rather low value of μh measured in the FET configuration (10−4 cm2 V−1 s−1) (Table 3). For this reason, following a general concept known in the literature,238 additional thiophene units bearing alkyl chains were incorporated into the backbone yielding p4.23A – an alternating copolymer of benzodithiophene and dialkylbithiophene with better solution processability. This polymer showed a π-stacking distance significantly shorter than that measured for p4.22. Its charge carrier mobility, calculated from the FET characteristics, improved by over one order of magnitude as compared to the case of p4.22, being still relatively low236 (2.1 × 10−3 cm2 V−1 s−1) (Table 3). According to the authors236 these rather moderate electrical parameters of thin films of p4.23A have their origin in an excessive number of solubilising groups per repeating unit which makes the formation of an organized supramolecular organization more difficult. A delicate compromise between the solubility and the capability of the supramolecularly ordered structure formation is needed. This was achieved by cutting the number of solubilising substituents by a factor of 2 (per repeating unit). Two polymers with reduced number of alkyl groups were prepared, namely p4.23B and p4.23C, in the former the two alkyl groups were attached to the benzene ring in the benzodithiophene moiety, whereas in the latter – to the bithiophene unit.236p4.23B is more soluble than p4.23C since its alkyl side groups can more freely rotate. This makes the deposition of thin layers of controlled supramolecular organization on appropriate substrates easier. p4.23C shows better charge carrier mobility in the FET measurements than p4.23B (0.134 cm2 V−1 s−1vs. 0.027 cm2 V−1 s−1) (Table 3). Interestingly, the presence of benzo[2,1-b:3,4-b′]dithiophene units introduces local curvature of the polymer, not perturbing its global linearity and the capability of forming ordered supramolecular structures through self-assembly. The shortest π-stacking distance of 0.37 nm is measured for p4.23C.236
Poly(2,8-bis-(3-tetradecylthiophene-2-yl)-5,12-bis(tetradecyl)dithienobenzothieno[3,2-b]thiophene) (p4.24) differs from the p4.21 by the extent of its fused aromatic segment. It was synthesized by Stille coupling polymerization with 2,8-bistrimethylstannyl-5,12-bis(tetradecyl)dithienobenzothieno[3,2-b]thiophene and 5,5′-dibromo-4,4′-bistetradecyl-2,2′-dithiophene using Pd(PPh3)4 as a catalyst in toluene.239 The authors demonstrated that a polymer consisting of a large unit of six fused rings with only two alkyl substituents which alternates with a dialkyl-bithiophene unit can still be soluble. Despite the fact that in the solid state p4.24 exhibits features characteristic of polymers of high μh, (a highly ordered, lamellar supramolecular structure with a short π-stacking distance, 0.37 nm), its hole mobility is disappointingly low (1.3 × 10−3 cm2 V−1 s−1) (Table 3), which indicates that optimizing redox and structural properties of a given conjugated polymer may not necessarily lead to the desired semiconducting properties in real devices.
Copolymers of benzothieno[3,2-b]benzothiophene (four unsubstituted fused rings segment) with dialkylbithiophenes are not well suited for FET or photovoltaic applications because of their twisted main chain (λmax for the π–π* transition <400 nm) and show no field effect in the p-channel configuration.240 Meanwhile, copolymers of their naphtho[1,2-b:5,6-b′]dithiophene analogues (p4.25A–E) which are isoelectronic with benzothieno[3,2-b]benzothiophene241 are very promising semiconductors for FETs,240 exhibiting FET hole mobilities in the range of 0.2 to 0.54 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.25B to p4.25Ei.e. polymers with a comparable molecular mass. One order of magnitude lower hole mobility was measured for p4.25A which showed 5 fold smaller molecular mass, consistent with the observation of a strong effect of Mn on the charge carrier mobility in conjugated polymeric semiconductors.72c
Osaka et al. in their detailed study investigated the effect of isomerism of the naphthodithiophene unit on the spectroscopic, structural and electrical transport properties of poly(2,7-bis(3-alkylthiophen-2-yl)-alt-naphtho[1,2-b:5,6-b′]dithiophene)s.242 Copolymers containing four different isomers of naphthodithiophene were compared: naphtho[1,2-b:5,6-b′]dithiophene (p4.25C and p4.25E), naphtho[2,1-b:6,5-b′]dithiophene (p4.26A and p4.26B), naphtho[2,3-b:6,7-b′]dithiophene (p4.27A and p4.27B), naphtho[2,3-b:7,6-b′]dithiophene (p4.28A and p4.28B). Alkyl groups of two different lengths (R = C16H33 or R = C20H41) were attached to the bithiophene unit to induce solubility. All copolymers were prepared by Stille coupling polymerization and showed comparable molecular mass and close values of IP, determined by photoelectron spectroscopy (from 5.2 eV for p4.28 to 5.0 eV p4.25). Judging from these values, polymers of all isomeric forms studied are suitable candidates for use as semiconductors in p-channel FETs. One should however be aware of the fact that the type of isomerism strongly influences the polymer chain geometry: in p4.25 it is pseudo-straight, in p4.26 it is sine-like, in p4.27 it adopts a zig-zag geometry whereas in p4.28 the chain geometry is square wave-like. These are local geometrical changes, the global chain linearity remains preserved in all cases. These local differences in the macromolecule geometry have a strong impact on the structural organization of thin polymer films. The grazing incidence X-ray diffraction (GIXRD) patterns show the best structural organization in p4.25, then in p4.26, p4.27 and p4.28 being less ordered, both in plane and out of plane. This trend in supramolecular organization is reflected in the FET hole mobilities measured for all isomeric forms. They decrease in the following sequence: p4.25 > p4.26 > p4.27 > p4.28 (Table 3). The discussed paper constitutes an instructive example of a careful chain polymer chain engineering in view of the optimization of the charge carrier mobility.
One of the drawbacks of thiophene- of benzothiophene-based semiconducting polymers is their IP values, which frequently are not sufficiently high to assure air operating stability or are close to its limiting value. To increase IP, electron accepting units are sometimes incorporated into the polymer main chain. Thiazole is one of the most popular electron-deficient groups used for this purpose. Several moieties of thiazole, such as bithiazole, thiazolothiazole and benzobisthiazole have been used in organic synthesis for a long time. Now, researchers have been continuing to explore some novel structures for enriching the library of thiazole-based molecules.243 Meanwhile, new preparation methods have been elaborated, which enabled the synthesis of thiazole containing compounds under milder conditions.244 Small molecules containing thiadiazole were used as n or p-type semiconductors in OFETs or as building blocks for the preparation of polymeric semiconductors.245
In the early years of the present century low molecular compounds consisting of thiophene and thiadiazole units have been tested as active layers in FETs, however yielding rather low hole mobilities.246 Yamamoto et al.247 synthesized an alternating copolymer of thiophene and alkylthiadiazole with an enhanced IP value (5.3 eV), improving air-operating stability. In thin layers the copolymer showed highly ordered lamellar-type supramolecular organization, similar to that of P3HT with an interchain distance of 2.65 nm and a π-stacking distance of 0.365 nm. Despite these promising features of the semiconducting polymer hole mobilities, measured in the FET configuration, were still low.

p4.29A and p4.29B, which can be considered as alternating copolymers of HH coupled dialkylbithiazole and TT coupled dialkylbithiophene, were obtained by Yamamoto dehalogenation polycondensation of the corresponding dibromotetramer (Scheme 12) using a zerovalent nickel complex.248 Both polymers showed increased IP values (5.15 eV and 5.20 eV) as compared to the case of P3HT. UV-vis spectra of thin layers showed a characteristic π–π* transition band of a distinct vibrational structure characteristic of polythiophene-based polymers of high conjugation length.179 The maxima of the vibrational peaks were however hypsochromically shifted as compared to the case of P3HT. Thin layers of p4.29A showed ordered supramolecular organization of lamellar type, similar to that found in thin layers of P3HT whereas layers of p4.29B were amorphous,248μh measured for p4.29A in the FET configuration gave a value of 0.015 cm2 V−1 s−1 whereas in p4.29B the field effect was hardly detectable because of the amorphous nature of its thin layers which impeded effective charge carrier transport.
 Scheme 12  Synthetic route to prepare p4.29. 
Poly(didodecylquaterthiophene-alt-didodecylbithiazole), p4.30, was prepared from the distannyl derivative of bithiophene and the dibromoderivative of 2,2′-bis(3-dodecylthiophene-2-yl)-4,4′didodecylthiophene-5,5′-bi-1,3-thiazole by Stille coupling polymerization.249 The presence of electron withdrawing thiazole rings in the polymer main chain increases its IP value to 5.19 eV, improving its stability against oxidation under air operating conditions. The polymer has liquid crystalline properties which facilitate the formation of highly ordered structure in thin films deposited on appropriate substrates. This supramolecular organization can be further improved by annealing. As evidenced by X-ray diffraction studies the macromolecules adopt the edge-on position with the π-stacking direction parallel to the substrate. The stacks are highly oriented as evidenced by ω-scans in the X-ray rocking mode. The π-stacking distance is 0.37 nm and the distance between the stacks separated by lateral alkyl substituents is 2.1 nm. This ordered supramoleular organization leads to the FET hole mobility value of 0.33 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3) for annealed films.
Paek et al.250 studied the effect of the presence of bithiazole groups on the spectroscopic, electrochemical, structural and electrical transport properties of an alternating polymer composed of tetraalkylated quaterthiophene and 2,2′-bithiazole units (p4.31) by a comparison with its “all thiophene” analogue. p4.31 was prepared by Stille coupling of 3,3′-didodecyl-5,5′-bis(trimethylstannyl)-2,2′-bithiophene and 5,5′-bis(5-bromo-4-dodecylthiophene-2-yl)-2,2′-bithiazole. The presence of electron withdrawing groups leads to a small increase of the IP value from 5.33 eV in the “all thiophene” polymer to 5.39 eV in p4.31. In the UV-vis spectrum of a thin solid film of p4.31 a bathochromic shift by 60 nm of the band ascribed to the π–π* transition can be noticed, indicating optical band gap lowering. Moreover, the “all thiophene” polymer was amorphous whereas the out-of-plane X-ray scattering pattern of p4.31 shows a set of four distinct reflections of the (h00) family yielding a d-spacing of 2.07 nm, which corresponds to the distance between π-conjugated main-chains separated by interdigitated alkyl substituents. Thus, thin films of p4.31 exhibit an ordered supramolecular organization typical of polymers with a stiff conjugated backbone containing flexible side chains. p4.31 is also a better semiconductor for the fabrication of FETs (and possibly PCs) showing the FET hole mobility of 1.1 × 10−3 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3) i.e. nearly two orders of magnitude higher than its “all thiophene” analogue.
A similar comparative study of polymers containing thiazole units with their “all thiophene” analogues was carried out by Kong et al.251 Before describing their results in detail, it is instructive to outline the possible interdigitation patterns characteristic of supramolecular organization in heterocyclic conjugated polymers containing alkyl side chains. Depending on the type of the side group distribution in a regiochemically well defined polymer chain, two types of interdigitations are possible: A-shaped and H-shaped (see Fig. 9). In general, ordered supramolecular organization is easier to achieve for H-shaped packed polymers such as poly(3,3′′′′-didodecylquaterthiophene) and poly(2,5-bis(3-alkylthiophene-2-yl)thieno[3,2-b]thiophene)201a,205,210,252 than for A-shaped packed ones which include, among others poly(3,3′′-didodecyl-2,2′:5′,2′′-terthiophene) and poly(2,5-bis(3-dodecylthiophen-2-yl)thieno[2,3-b]thiophene).200,226,253
Two polymers were designed:251 poly(5,5′-bis(3′,4-didodecyl-2,2′-bithiophen-5-yl)-2,2′-bithiazole) (p4.32) and poly(5,5′-bis(2,5′-(thiophene-2,5-diyl)bis(3-dodecylthiophene)-5-yl)-2,2′-bithiazole) (p4.33), which are A- and H-shaped packed, respectively. They were prepared by Stille coupling polymerization in the presence of Pd2(dba)3 and P(o-tol)3. For comparison their “all thiophene” analogues were also prepared. The obtained results were in line with the general trends observed for heterocyclic conjugated polymers. First, the incorporation of the thiazole unit resulted in a small increase of the IP value – higher for p4.32 (0.11 eV) than for p4.33 (0.06 eV), which was consistent with a higher ratio of thiazole to thiophene ring in the former. Second, a large bathochromic shift of the π–π* transition band was observed for both polymers containing thiazole units, indicating lowering of the optical band gap. Thiazole containing polymers exhibited better thermal stability and more ordered supramolecular organization as evidenced by out-of-plane and in-plane X-ray diffraction patterns. In line with its most ordered supramolecular structure p4.33 showed the highest FET hole mobility (0.05 cm2 V−1 s−1) (Table 3) and the highest power conversion efficiency (PCE) of 1.39%, when used as a component of bulk heterojunction photovoltaic cells.
Recently, Guo et al.254 have proposed HH coupled dialkoxy-bithiazoles as building blocks for semiconducting conjugated polymers. In poly(alkylthiophenes) the presence of HH coupled dyads usually induced the chain torsion which led to an increase of IP to values unexploitable for p-channel FETs. Moreover, the resulting polymers usually showed a poor supramolecular organization.195 This is not the case for HH coupling of alkoxythiazoles since small oxygen van der Waals radius together with intramolecular S(thiazolyl)⋯O(alkoxy) attraction improve the planarity of the HH coupled dyad. The synthetic pathways leading to 4,4′-bis(dodecoxy)-5,5′-bithiazole and p4.34, its homopolymer, as well as p4.35, its copolymer with TT coupled dialkylbithiophene, are depicted in Scheme 13. Thin films of both polymers show good structural organization and high hole mobility in the FET configuration (0.15 and 0.25 cm2 V−1 s−1, respectively) (Table 3). Their IP values are 4.94 eV and 4.80 eV i.e. lower than that of P3HT. This is caused by the fact that the electron withdrawing effect of the thiazole ring is overbalanced by the electron donating effect of the alkoxy substituent.
 Scheme 13  Synthetic routes to prepare p4.34 and p4.35. 
To summarize, bithiazole derivatives seem to be promising building blocks for the preparation of semiconducting polymers with a variety of comonomers, not necessarily from the oligothiophene family.
Osaka et al.255 reported a series of alternating copolymers of tetra-alkylated quaterthiophene with fused bithiazole which differed in the length of the alkyl lateral groups (p4.36A–C). Similarly to other polymers containing thiophene and thiazole units, they can be considered as donor–acceptor copolymers. The thiazolo-thiazole containing comonomers were prepared by the reaction of the corresponding aldehyde and dithiooxamide (Scheme 14), poly(2,5-bis(3-alkyl-5-(3-alkylthiophen-2-yl)thiophen-2-yl)thiazolo[5,4-d]thiazole)s (p4.36A–C) were synthesized by Stille coupling polymerization (Scheme 14). A drawback of these polymers is their relatively low Mn value.
 Scheme 14  Synthetic route to prepare p4.36C. 
The presence of the thiazolo-thiazole unit in p4.36A–C increases their IP and lowers their optical band gap as compared to P3HT. Taking into account their polymer chain structure, they cannot form T-shaped interdigitation patterns but rather a kind of A-shaped ones. Despite this fact, they self-assemble in thin films, forming an ordered supramolecular organization of lamellar type which improves with increasing length of the lateral, alkyl substituent. For p4.36Cμh in the FET configuration reaches 0.3 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3).
A series of copolymers (p4.37, p4.38, p4.39) containing the same thiazolo[5,4-d]thiazole units as in the p4.36 but with higher ratios of electron accepting to electron donating units were synthesized by Stille coupling polymerization.256 Consistent with their chemical structure, IP values of p4.37, p4.38 and p4.39 (5.2–5.3 eV) were found to be 0.1–0.2 eV higher than that of p4.36. In thin films these polymers showed less ordered supramolecular organization than p4.36C, typical of distorted lamellae. This is probably caused by the branched nature of the substituents. With an exception of p4.37 they showed FET mobilities reaching 0.1 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3). Excellent FET air-operating stability of this polymer series should be pointed out, consistent with their deepened HOMO level (increased IP).

p4.40 and p4.41 being alternating copolymers of thiazolo[5,4-d]thiazole and tetraalkylated quaterthiophene are chemically similar to p4.36 but differ from it by the distribution pattern of the alkyl substituent along the polymer chain. Both polymers were synthesized by Stille coupling polymerization.257 The authors studied the effect of their regiochemical environment on the spectroscopic, redox and electrical transport properties. The only difference between the chemical structure of both polymers lies in one sequence of coupling (HH in p4.40 and HT in p4.41, see the substituent labeled in red). The HH coupling induces a significant torsion angle in the polymer chain of p4.40 which leads to an increased value of its IP value (5.6 eV) as compared to the case of p4.41 whose IP is equal to 5.3 eV. A hypsochromic shift in the π–π* transition band, from 560 nm for p4.41 to 520 nm for p4.40, is also observed for thin solid films. Layers of both polymers on an SiO2 covered Si substrate are amorphous. This probably accounts for rather low μh values measured in the FET configuration (0.02 cm2 V−1 s−1) (Table 3). Both polymers were also tested in organic PC as components of bulk heterojunctions in combination with methanofullerene[6,6]-phenyl C71-butyric acid methyl ester (PC71BM). A power conversion efficiency (PCE) of 2.70% was reached for p4.40.
Poly(benzobisthiazole-alt-3-octylquarterthiophene) (p4.42) reported by Ahmed et al.258 is somehow similar to p4.36 having a benzobisthiazole electron accepting group instead of a thiazolo-thiazole one. 2,6-Bis(3-octylthiophen-2-yl)-benzo[1,2-d;4,5-d′]bisthiazole, the comonomer containing benzobisthiazole, was prepared by acid-catalyzed condensation of 3-octylthiophene-2-carboxylaldehyde and 2,5-diamino-1,4-benzenedithiol dihydrochloride259 and then reacted with the distannyl derivative of dialkylbithiophene to yield p4.42 through Stille coupling (Scheme 15).260 Similarly like in the case of poly(alkylthiophene)-type homopolymers72c,179 its spectroscopic, redox and electrical transport properties are molecular mass dependent. IP of the polymer fraction showing Mn = 8000 g mol−1 is 5.2 eV, a value comparable to that measured for p4.36 of similar molecular mass. X-ray diffraction studies of thin films reveal the presence of the (h00) family of reflections corresponding to an interlayer lamellar d100-spacing of 1.56 nm, much shorter than the corresponding distance in poly(3-alkylthiophene) with the same (octyl) lateral substituent. This seems to indicate a higher degree of alkyl chains interdigitation in p4.42. The FET hole mobility measured for the fraction of Mn = 8000 g mol−1 is rather low (0.002 cm2 V−1 s−1) and increases only 5 fold for 40 times higher Mn. A low molecular mass fraction of p4.42 (8000 g mol−1) in combination with PC71BM was also tested as a component of BHJ in organic photovoltaic cells, yielding a PCE value of 2.1%.258
 Scheme 15  Synthetic route to prepare p4.42. 

p4.43 and p4.44 which also contain a benzobisthiazole group in their repeating unit were synthesized through the conventional Stille coupling polymerization.261 Their similarity to p4.39 should be pointed out. p4.43 is easier to solution process. It is soluble in chloroform and chlorinated benzenes even at room temperature, p4.44 is soluble in warm chlorinated benzenes. Their IP is high and comparable to that of p4.39 (5.3 eV and 5.2 eV for p4.43 and p4.44, respectively). Solution-cast thin films of both polymers show ordered supramolecular organization with a short π-stacking distance of 0.36 nm. A comparison of the in-plane and out of plane diffraction patterns indicates that the lamellae are edge-on oriented on the substrate surface. The measured hole mobilities in the FET configuration reach 0.18 and 0.26 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3), for p4.43 and p4.44, respectively. High air operating stability of both polymeric semiconductors should be pointed out.
First reports on the use of N-alkyldithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrroles as fused aromatic building blocks were published by Ogawa et al.262 These monomers show a completely flat crystal structure, which is a clear manifestation of good π conjugation across the condensed rings. N-alkyldithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrroles can be chemically (FeCl3) or electrochemically polymerized to yield poly(N-alkyldithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrroles), exhibiting excellent stability in their oxidized (polycarbocation or doped) state. This stability in the conducting form arises from its low IP value, much lower than that of P3HT and comparable to that of poly(ethylenedioxythiophene). In addition to their low IP poly(N-alkyldithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrroles) have low band gaps.263 Low IP constitutes a serious drawback of all N-alkyldithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrrole-containing conjugated polymers because it excludes their use as semiconductors under air operating conditions. However, even when working in an inert atmosphere they show low on/off ratios due to the difficulty in the complete removal of all permanent charge carriers, originating from the oxidative doping. These permanent charges interfere with the ones created by the field effect in FETs or in PCs with the charges originating from excitons dissociation.264
Liu et al.265 synthesized a series of soluble alternating copolymers of N-alkyldithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrrole and thiophene or bithiophene (p4.45, p4.46 and p4.47) by Stille coupling copolymerization. Different thiophene comonomers were used: 3-alkylthiophenes (p4.45), 3,4-didodecylthiophene (p4.46) and 4,4′-didodecyl-2,2′-bithiophene (p4.47A), 3,3′-dihexyl-2,2′-bithiophene (p4.47B) (Scheme 16). p4.45(A–D), p4.46 and p4.47A have band gaps between 1.74 and 1.84 eV, which are smaller than that of regioregular P3HT. The lowering of the bands gaps originates from a more coplanar structure of the polymer and the donor–acceptor effect of dithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrrole and thiophene. For the regioirregular polymers, p4.45(A–D), which have a 1:1 ratio of thiophene/dithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrrole units in the polymer backbone, the band gaps are the lowest (between 1.74 and 1.79 eV). As expected, the IP values of all synthesized copolymers are also low, as determined by cyclic voltammetry.265 The highest IP is determined for p4.47B in which dithieno[3,2-b:2′,3′-d]pyrrole units alternate with HH linked dialkyl-substituted thiophene rings. Among all as-cast samples, p4.47A exhibited the best field effect performance with the highest FET hole mobility of 0.21 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3), the value which is higher than the highest FET hole mobility reported for regioregular poly(3-hexylthiophene).266 Interestingly, after thermal annealing at 120 °C for 30 min, the mobilities of all the samples decreased, in some cases by as much as one order of magnitude. All transistor testing had to be carried out in argon, but even under these conditions the obtained on/off ratios were low.
 Scheme 16  Synthetic route to prepare p4.45. 
Conjugated building blocks containing silicon substituents constitute an interesting option for the preparation of semiconducting polymers. Such substituents are known to stabilize adjacent carbanionic centers due to the effective hyperconjugation between negatively charged carbon centers and the adjacent silyl groups.267 Among the various systems being considered, silole (sila-2,4-cyclopentadiene) containing polymers have attracted significant attention as systems in which the exocyclic Si–C σ*-orbital effectively mixes with the π*-orbital of the butadiene fragment to afford a low-lying lowest-unoccupied molecular orbital (LUMO) and a relatively small band gap.268 Additionally, the silole bridge better stabilizes the diene HOMO level compared to the carbon analogues.268b This effect should enhance the stability of FETs fabricated from silole-containing polymers under ambient operating conditions.
Lu et al.269 reported the synthesis of 3,3′-dihexylsilylene-2,2′-bithiophene-based homopolymer, p4.48 and, and its copolymers with thiophene or bithiophene (p4.49A and p4.49B). The synthetic pathway leading to p4.48 is presented in Scheme 17. All polymers have excellent thermal and environmental stability. p4.48 showed no field effect, probably due to two reasons: amorphous structure in thin layers and too high (5.6 eV) IP value which constituted a substantial hole injection barrier. p4.49A and p4.49B exhibited lower IP values (5.2 eV and 5.3 eV) and an ordered supramolecular organization in thin layers. Both were found to be promising p-channel semiconductors, yielding a FET hole mobility of 0.05 cm2 V−1 s−1 and 0.08 cm2 V−1 s−1, respectively (Table 3).
 Scheme 17  Synthetic route to prepare p4.48. 
The dibromo derivative of dibenzosilole is another building block used for the synthesis of silole-containing conjugated polymers. Its synthetic pathway is depicted in Scheme 18. p4.50A and p4.50B were prepared269 through Suzuki polycondensation between 2,7-dibromo-9,9-dioctyldibenzosilole (Scheme 18)270 and 2,5-bis(4,4,5,5-tetramethyl-1,3,2-dioxaborolan-2-yl)thiophene (p4.50A) and 2,5′-bis(4,4,5,5-tetramethyl-1,3,2-dioxaborolan-2-yl)bithiophene (p4.50B). These polymers are only soluble in chlorinated aromatic solvents such as warm chlorobenzene, dichlorobenzene and trichlorobenzene, which is probably a consequence of their higher molecular masses (Table 3). As evidenced by X-ray diffraction studies they adopt similar supramolecular structure to p4.49A and p4.49B, however less ordered as judged from more pronounced broadening of the Bragg reflections. As a consequence the FET hole mobilities 6 × 10−5 cm2 V−1 s−1 and 6 × 10−3 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.50A and p4.50B, respectively, are lower than those measured for p4.49A and p4.49B (Table 3).269
 Scheme 18  Synthetic route to prepare 2,7-dibromo-9,9-dialkylsilafluorene. 

p4.51A and p4.51Bi.e. fluorene analogues of p4.50A and p4.50B were studied more than a decade ago by Sirringhaus et al.271p4.51B synthesized by Suzuki coupling272 showed liquid crystallinity and better FET charge carrier mobilities (0.01–0.02 cm2 V−1 s−1) than that reported for p4.50B as well as good operating stability. A slightly lower μh for p4.51B (0.006 cm2 V−1 s−1) was reported in ref. 269.
Alternating copolymers of fluorenone and oligothiophenes were also studied.79,273 Replacement of the fluorene moiety (p4.51) by the fluorenone one (p4.52) improves the thermal stability of the polymer, increases its IP and lowers the band gap since the polymer becomes donor–acceptor (–DA–) in nature. p4.54 contains three types of chromophores, being in conjugation: fluorenone, thiophene and vinylene. The π–π* band in the UV-vis-NIR spectra of p4.53 and p4.54 is shifted towards the NIR (absorption edge above 700 nm), which is a clear consequence of their low band gap. Both polymers exhibiting p-type conductivity were tested as components of bulk heterojunction photovoltaic cells together with PC61BM, yielding power conversion efficiencies of 1.5% and 1.1% for p4.53 and p4.54, respectively.
Thieno[3,4-c]pyrrole-4,6-dione is another electron accepting building block which has been widely used for the preparation of p-type organic semiconductors for FETs and PCs.274 The presence of this moiety in copolymers with more electron rich comonomers like thiophene oligomers, for example, lowers both the HOMO and the LUMO levels of the resulting macromolecular compounds, the former being however much more affected. Using these copolymers high open circuit voltages (0.8–1.0 V) and good power conversion efficiencies (3–7%) can be obtained for bulk heterojunction photovoltaic cells.274 In FETs low-lying HOMO levels (high IPs) improve air operating stability of the devices.258,269,275 However, the IP values cannot be too high because in this case hole injection may become difficult as observed for semiconductors with IP > 5.5 eV. A delicate balance is needed here.276
Guo et al.277 reported the synthesis of a homopolymer of thieno[3,4-c]pyrrole-4,6-dione), p4.55, and a series of its copolymers with thiophene or its oligomers (p4.56–p4.59). The main building block for these copolymers i.e. 1,3-dibromo-5-N-alkylthieno[3,4-c]pyrrole-4,6-dione (Scheme 19) was first synthesized by Zhang et al.278 This original procedure was then modified by Nielsen and Bjørnholm.279 In recent years the preparation of this building block has been significantly facilitated by the commercial availability of thiophene-3,4-dicarboxylic acid.274a Thus, this reagent is first converted into the anhydride and then into the imide. The imidization reaction cannot be in this case achieved under conditions typically employed in the preparation of phthalimides280 or naphthalene diimides.117 but a two-step procedure has to be used. After reaction with the appropriate amines in toluene, the anhydride is converted to the corresponding 4-alkylcarbamoylthiophene-3-carboxylic acid, which then undergoes the SOCl2 assisted imidization without further purification.277 Dibromination with NBS is the final step of the precursor preparation. Its Yamamoto coupling leads to the homopolymer (p4.55) (Scheme 19). The copolymers (p4.56–p4.59) were synthesized by Stille coupling.135
 Scheme 19  Synthetic route to prepare p4.55. 
The alkyl substituent in the thieno[3,4-c]pyrrole-4,6-dione unit assures very good solubilities of p4.59D and p4.59E up to 40 mg mL−1 in solvents such as chloroform, hexane, toluene. p4.55 shows limited π-conjugation as evidenced by its π–π* band in the UV-vis spectrum which is hypsochromically shifted with respect to the same bands of polymers of the same family. No field effect in neither n- nor in p-configuration was measured for p4.55. This can, at least in part, be associated with the amorphous character of its thin films. p4.56–p4.59 are better conjugated since repulsive imide–imide interactions, causing the polymer chain torsion, are weakened by the presence of thiophene spacers. p4.56 which has the highest ratio of the thieno[3,4-c]pyrrole-4,6-dione unit to the thiophene ring exhibits ambipolar behavior under vacuum with electron and hole mobilities of ∼10−4–10−3 cm2 V−1 s−1. All other copolymers of this family (p4.57, p4.58 and p4.59) show field effect only in the p-channel configuration with hole mobilities approaching or surpassing 0.1 cm2 V−1 s−1 – the highest being measured for p4.58 (0.6 cm2 V−1 s−1) (Table 3). In p4.57B the lowest band gap is determined which is associated with the electron-donating properties of the alkoxy substituent. However, the presence of these substituents has a negative impact on the air-operating stability of p4.57B since its IP becomes lower than the IP of P3HT.277 As evidenced by X-ray diffraction studies, the supramolecular organization of copolymers containing oligoalkylthiophene units is similar to that of poly(alkylthiophenes) and governed by π-stacking and interdigitation of side alkyl chains.
Compounds containing diketopyrrolopyrrole chromophores have been often used as components of organic pigments,281 and their solubility can be improved by appropriate modification of their chemical constitution.282 Diketopyrrolopyrrole can also be used as a building block of organic semiconducting polymers with tunable electronic properties.136 Three copolymers containing diketopyrrolopyrrole units have already been discussed in Section 3 as instructive examples of the design of tailor-made polymers exhibiting tunable spectroscopic and electronic properties. The diketopyrrolopyrrole unit exhibits a planar conjugated bicyclic structure, which favors conjugation. Its copolymers with more electron rich comonomers show low band gaps and are very well suited for the fabrication of bulk heterojunction PCs with thiophene or its oligomers. Typical comonomers used for the preparation of alternating copolymers with diketopyrrolopyrrole are dibenzosilole, benzodithiophene, dithienosilole or substituted bithiophenes.139,147,282b,283
Using 3,6-bis(5-bromothiophene-2-yl)-2,5-bis(2-hexyldecyl)-2,5-dihydropyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrole-1,4-dione, whose synthetic pathway is presented in Scheme 20, Burgi et al. synthesized poly[3,6-bis-(4′-dodecyl-[2,2′]bithiophenyl-5-yl)-2,5-bis-(2-hexyldecyl)-2,5-dihydropyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrole-1,4-dione] (p4.60), through Yamamoto coupling.138 The π–π* absorption band of p4.60 is located in the NIR part of the spectrum, being indicative of a low band gap. The high value of IP for this polymer, in combination with a low band gap leads to a rather high |EA| value of 4.0 eV. This polymer is therefore almost ideally suited for the fabrication of one-component ambipolar FETs. Indeed, in the FET configuration p4.60 shows well balanced hole and electron mobilities of 0.1 cm2 V−1 s−1 and 0.09 cm2 V−1 s−1, respectively (Table 3). Light emitting FETs can be fabricated from p4.60 which under appropriate bias emit near-infrared light. This property is inherently associated with ambipolar character of this polymer.138
 Scheme 20  Synthetic pathway leading to the dibromo-derivative of 3,6-bis(thiophen-2-yl)-2,5-bis(2-hexyldecyl)-2,5-dihydropyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrole-1,4-dione. 

p4.61 is an alternating copolymer of diketopyrrolopyrrole and unsubstituted terthiophene.283c It can be synthesized from the 3,6-bis(5-bromo-2-thienyl)-2,5-dihydro-2,5-di(2-hexyldecyl)-pyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrolo-1,4-dione and bis(4,4,5,5-tetramethyl-1,3-dioxaborolane)-2,5-thiophene by Suzuki polymerization. Its molecular mass depends on the type of the used catalyst. The application of Pd2(dba)3/PPh3 as a catalyst yielded p4.61 of Mn = 54000 g mol−1 whereas a much lower Mn of 10000 g mol−1 was obtained using a Pd(PPh3)4 catalyst.146 The optical band gap of p4.61 is small (1.36 eV measured for thin solid films). The high molecular mass polymer (Mn = 54000 g mol−1) was ambipolar in the FET configuration and exhibited hole and electron mobilities of 0.04 and 0.01 cm2 V−1 s−1 respectively (Table 3). Surprisingly, these mobilities were found to be almost independent of the molecular mass.146 In combination with phenyl-C70-butyric acid methyl ester (PC70BM), high molecular mass p4.61 was tested as a component of a bulk heterojunction PC reaching external power conversion efficiency η = 4.7%. In contrast to Mn independent FET mobility, a dramatic reduction in organic photovoltaic cell performance was observed when the high molecular polymer was replaced by the low Mn one, processed under identical conditions.146

p4.62 differs from p4.61 by the presence of a phenyl ring in its aromatic segment. The immediate effect of this change on the redox properties of the copolymer is an increase of IP from 5.17 eV in p4.61 to 5.35 eV in p4.62 and of the optical band gap from 1.36 eV to 1.53 eV. Similarly to p4.61, p4.62 is ambipolar, showing electron and hole FET mobilities of 0.02 and 0.01 cm2 V−1 s−1, respectively (Table 3). In combination with phenyl-C70-butyric acid methyl ester (PC70BM) it can also serve as a component of efficient PCs, showing power conversion efficiencies of 5.5%.147
Poly[2,5-bis(2-octyldodecyl)pyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrole-1,4(2H,5H)dione-alt-2,2′:5′,2′′:5′′,2′′′′-quaterthiophene] (p4.63) and poly[2,5-bis(2-octyldodecyl)pyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrole-1,4(2H,5H)dione-alt-5,5′-di(thiophenyl-2-yl)-2,2′-biselenophene] (p4.64) were synthesized in high yields using Stille coupling polymerization.284 Excellent solubility (up to 12 mg mL−1) of both polymers in organic solvents such as chloroform, dichloromethane, toluene, THF, and chlorobenzene should be pointed out. A small optical band gap of 1.32–1.29 eV was measured for both polymers. They did not exhibit ambipolarity and in test FETs always behaved as p-conductors showing, after annealing, very high hole mobilities of 1.04 cm2 V−1 s−1 and 1.50 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.63 and p4.64, respectively (Table 3).284a It was found by X-ray diffraction that p4.64 exhibited a slightly denser packing than p4.63. The latter exhibited an interesting morphology of its thin films characterized by uniform, densely packed intertwined polymer fibers. As in the case of polythiophene homopolymers its FET mobility was found to be molecular mass dependent.284b
Lee et al.285 reported the synthesis of p4.65B – a copolymer of 3,6-bis(thiophen-2-yl)-2,5-dihydropyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrole-1,4-dione with two siloxane substituents at the nitrogen atoms alternating with selenophene. Its preparation started from a standard N-alkylation of dithienyl-diketopyrrolopyrrole with 6-bromo-1-hexane under basic conditions. Subsequent hydrosilylation reaction of the olefinic compound 3,6-di(thien-2-yl)-2,5-di(hexy-5-en-1-yl)-pyrrolo[3,4-c]pyrrole-1,4-dione using 1,1,1,3,5,5,5-heptamethyltrisiloxane gave the siloxane-substituted precursor in the presence of a Karstedt catalyst.286 This precursor was then converted to the dibrominated dithienyl-diketopyrrolopyrrole. A Stille copolymerization of the dibrominated dithienyl-diketopyrrolopyrrole and distannylated selenophene yielded p4.65B. The main goal of the introduction of the siloxane substituent was to enhance the copolymer compatibility with the OTS modified SiO2/Si substrate. Therefore a dithienyl-diketopyrrolopyrrole selenophene copolymer with 2-octyldodecyl substituents (p4.65A) was also prepared for comparative reasons. Both polymers turned out to be ambipolar. The effect of the siloxane groups was very pronounced since p4.65B showed, after annealing, very high hole and electron mobilities of 3.97 and 2.20 cm2 V−1 s−1, respectively, measured in the FET configuration. Identically processed layers of p4.65A showed lower hole and electron mobilities: 2.53 cm2 V−1 s−1 and 0.43 cm2 V−1 s−1.285
Naphthylene cyclopentadienone has also been proposed as an electron accepting group in the design of alternating copolymers with oligothiophenes. A series of polymeric semiconductors containing this moiety was reported.287p4.66, a copolymer of dialkylquaterthiophene and naphthylene cyclopentadienone was prepared following the reactions sequence depicted in Scheme 21. 1,3-Dithienyl-2-propanone was prepared by self-condensation of thiopheneacetic acid using DCC (dicyclohexylcarbodiimide) and DMA (4-dimethylaminopyridine).288 The dithienylcyclopentadienone derivative was then synthesized via a double Knoevenagel condensation with acenenaphthenequinone.289 2,5-Di(5-bromothienyl)-3,4-(1,8-napthylene)cyclopentadienone was obtained after treatment with bromine in acetic acid/dichloromethane. The Stille cross-coupling polymerization of 2,5-di(5-bromothienyl)-3,4-(1,8-naphthylene)cyclopentadienone with 4,4′-dihexyl[2,2′]bithiophene or 4,4′-didodecyl[2,2′]bithiophene yielded p4.66A and p4.66B.287b Both polymers show interesting UV-vis-NIR spectra consisting of two overlapping bands. The higher energetic band with a clear maximum at wavelengths below 500 nm is located at approximately the same position as the corresponding band in dithienylcyclopentadienone which can be ascribed to the π–π* transition in naphthylene cyclopentadienone. The second band exhibits its λmax in the NIR (at 767 and 806 nm for p4.66A and p4.66B, respectively). Organic semiconducting NIR-absorbing materials are rare and are of significant technological interest.5p4.66A and p4.66B exhibit field effects in the p-channel configuration with the FET hole mobilities of 7.8 × 10−3 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.66A and 2.26 × 10−2 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.66B (Table 3).
 Scheme 21  Synthetic route to prepare 2,5-di(5-bromothienyl)-3,4-(1,8-naphthylene)cyclopentadienone. 
Several alternating copolymers of pyrazine and oligothiophenes showing tunable band gap were synthesized290 and tested as components of bulk heterojunction photovoltaic cells.291 Mondal et al.292 reported the synthesis of a series of copolymers consisting of alternating fused aromatic thieno[3,4-b]pyrazine (or [3,4-b]quinoxaline) and tetraalkylquaterthiophene units. The synthetic route to prepare these polymers is presented in Scheme 22. Condensation between the 3,4-diaminothiophene dihydrochloric acid salt and 1,2-acenaphthoquinone (or 9,10-phenanthenequinone) yields fused aromatic thienopyrazines acenaphtho[1,2-b]thieno[3,4-e]pyrazine and dibenzo[f,h]thieno[3,4-b]quinoxaline, respectively.293 Stille coupling between 8,10-bis(5-bromo-3-dodecylthiophen-2-yl)acenaphtho[1,2-e]thieno[3,4-b]pyrazine, 8,10-bis[5-bromo-3-(2-ethylhexyl)-thiophen-2-yl]acenaphtho[1,2-e]thieno[3,4-b]pyrazine or 10,12-bis[5-bromo-3-(2-ethylhexyl)-thiophen-2-yl]dibenzo[f,h]thieno[3,4-b]quinoxaline with (3,3′-didodecyl-2,2′-bithiophene-5,5′-diyl)bis(trimethylstannane) leads to p67A, p67B or p68 respectively. It should be noted that the band gap of these polymers, being in the range of 1.15 eV to 1.64 eV, better matches the solar spectrum than the gaps of heterocyclic homopolymers which do not contain electron accepting moieties. In the FET configuration all polymers of this family behave like p-type conductors, exhibiting moderate hole mobility approaching 10−2 cm2 V−1 s−1, in the best case (Table 3).
 Scheme 22  Synthetic route to prepare 8,10-bis(5-bromo-3-alkylthiophen-2-yl)acenaphtho[1,2-e]thieno[3,4-b]pyrazine. 
Strongly electron deficient isoindigo ((E)-1H,1H′-[3,3′]bindolylidene-2,2′-dione) is a fused planar aromatic conjugated molecule consisting of two indole heterocycles which are joined together in E-configuration via a central carbon–carbon double bond. Isoindigo based oligomers were first investigated by Mei et al.294 and showed promising absorption spectra and favorable electrochemical and photovoltaic properties. This finding stimulated growing research interest and in the past three years the dibromoderivative of isoindigo was used as a building block in the preparation of its alternating copolymers with thiophene and its oligomers, thienothiophenes, benzodithiophenes, acenes, fluorenes and carbazoles, to name only the most important.295 These copolymers were mainly used as donor (p-type conducting) components of bulk heterojunction photovoltaic cells, with PC71BM as an accepting phase, yielding sometimes very promising results like, for example, an efficiency of 6.3% for a copolymer consisting of alternating terthiophene and isoindigo units.295h
Lei et al.296 synthesized two alternating copolymers of isoindigo and thiophene (p4.69) and bithiophene (p4.70A). Direct condensation of two commercially available compounds, namely 6-bromoisatin and 6-bromooxindole, in acetic acid afforded 6,6′-dibromisoindigo in 86% yield (Scheme 23). Subsequently, 6,6′-dibromoisoindigo was alkylated with 1-iodo-2-octyldodecane to give 6,6′-dibromo-N,N′-(2-octyldodecanyl)isoindigo in 74% yield (Scheme 23). This bromoderivative of alkylated isoindigo constituted a convenient building block for the preparation of the targeted copolymers. Its Stille coupling polymerization with bis(trimethylstannyl)thiophene or 5,5′-bis(trimethylstannyl)-2,2′-bithiophene gave p4.69 and p4.70A, respectively. Both polymers showed similar redox properties, although the IP value of p4.70A (5.7 eV) was slightly lower than that of p4.69 (5.8 eV), consistent with a higher ratio of electron donating (thiophene) units to the electron-accepting (isoindigo) ones. Both polymers show a relatively high |EA| of 3.8 (p4.69) and 3.7 eV (p4.70A, Table 3), in line with their chemical constitution. As spun p4.69 did not exhibit observable field effect. However, after annealing at 150 °C, a hole mobility of 0.019 cm2 V−1 s−1 was measured in the FET configuration (Table 3). As evidenced by grazing incidence X-ray diffraction studies, thin layers of annealed p4.70A, showed a highly ordered supramolecular organization with edge-on lamellar packing of the molecules. As a result of this ordered structure, good hole mobilities were observed in the FET configuration, up to 0.79 cm2 V−1 s−1 (Table 3). This better performance of p4.70A as compared to p4.69 was not only attributed to its better structural organization but also to its higher molecular mass.296 As already indicated, in conjugated polymers μh is strongly dependent on Mn.72c,297 It should also be noted that devices fabricated from p4.70A were stable at high humidity for 1 month, evidently due to the high value of IP.
 Scheme 23  Synthetic route to prepare 6,6′-dibromo-N,N′-(alkyl)isoindigo. 
It is instructive to comment on the high value of IP for p4.69 (5.8 eV) and p4.70A (5.7 eV) which should make injection of holes difficult. However no such problems are encountered since the FET performance of both polymers was very good. Mei et al.298 also synthesized p4.70A and measured its IP by a direct method, namely photoelectron spectroscopy, providing a much lower value of 5.38 eV, whereas in ref. 299 a value of 5.54 eV was obtained by photoelectron spectroscopy. The lower IP fully explains the observed facility of hole injection. In view of these findings “electrochemical” values of IP in p4.70A should be treated with caution because usually differences between the “electrochemical” and “photoelectron” IP values are lower.84,85 This discrepancy may originate from inappropriate determination of the redox couple potential with respect to the reference electrode.
Copolymers with branched substituents longer than 2-octyldodecyl were also synthesized by Stille coupling polymerization, namely with 3-decyltridecyl (p4.70B), 4-decyltetradecyl (p4.70C) and 5-decylpentadecyl (p4.70D) groups.299 A fair correlation between the “electrochemical” and “photoelectron” values of IP was found. Thin layers of all three polymers exhibited long-range ordered edge-on lamellar packing with a short π-stacking distance of 0.361 nm for p4.70B and 0.357 nm for p4.70C and p4.70D. Thin films of p4.70C and p4.70D showed higher hole mobilities in the FET configuration than films of p4.70B (3.62 cm2 V−1 s−1 and 1.76 cm2 V−1 s−1vs. 0.40 cm2 V−1 s−1) but this was probably associated with more than twice higher Mn of the former, especially in view of the fact that the structural organization in all these cases is similar.
Mei et al.298 synthesized p4.70E which contained siloxane groups in its N-substituent. Similar siloxane-containing side groups were also introduced into p4.65B to improve its compatibility with the SiO2 substrate (vide supra). The synthesis of this polymer started from 2,6-dibromoisoindigo which was N-alkylated with an alkene-terminated linear alkyl chain.294 Hydrosilylation of the terminal alkene with 1,1,1,3,5,5,5-heptamethyltrisiloxane was then carried out in the presence of a commercially available Karstedt catalyst, yielding a highly soluble isoindigo monomer with siloxane-terminated solubilizing side chains.286p4.70E was synthesized from this monomer by microwave assisted Stille coupling with 5,5′-bis(trimethylstannyl)-2,2′-bithiophene.296 By photoelectron spectroscopy p4.70E showed a lower IP value (5.20 eV) than p4.70A (5.38 eV).145 This polymer turned out to be very well suited for the fabrication of FETs with SiO2 dielectric. Hole mobility approaching 2.5 cm2 V−1 s−1 was measured for annealed films (Table 3). Two key factors contribute to these excellent electrical transport properties of p70E: a very short π–π stacking distance of 0.358 nm and its better compatibility with the SiO2 substrate.298
Alternating copolymers of isoindigo and acenes, namely poly[N,N′-(2-octyldodecyl)isoindigo-alt-naphthalene] (p4.71) and poly[N,N′-(2-octyldodecyl)isoindigo-alt-anthracene] (p4.72), were synthesized by Sonar et al.300 The polymerization reaction involved Suzuki coupling of 6,6′-dibromo-N,N′-(2-octyldodecyl)isoindigo and 2,6-bis(4,4,5,5-tetramethyl-1,3,2-dioxaborolan-2-yl)naphthalene (or 2,6-bis(4,4,5,5-tetramethyl-1,3,2-dioxaborolan-2-yl)anthracene) respectively. The resulting polymers showed a high value of Mn (74000 g mol−1 and 52000 g mol−1 for p4.71 and p4.72, respectively). An excellent agreement was found for the “electrochemical” and “photoelectron” IP values which were close to 5.50 eV, high enough to assure air operating stability and low enough to assure efficient injection of holes. Both copolymers exhibited p-channel charge transport characteristics with the hole mobility measured in the FET configuration of 1.3 × 10−2 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.72 and 4.0 × 10−3 cm2 V−1 s−1 for p4.71 (Table 3). Owing to rather low optical band gaps (1.80 eV for p4.71 and 1.75 eV for p4.72) these polymers could be used as donors with a PC71BM acceptor in a bulk heterojunction PC, yielding a power conversion efficiency of 1.13% for p4.72 and 0.34% for p4.71.300
Benzothiadiazole has also been studied as an electron accepting unit in copolymers with thiophene or its oligomers. Semiconducting polymers of this type were mainly tested as components of bulk heterojunction PCs.301p4.73 – a copolymer of benzothiadiazole and dialkylquaterthiophene – was synthesized via Stille copolymerization from 4,7-bis(2-trimethylstannylthien-5-yl)-2,1,3-benzothiadiazole and 5,5′-dibromo-4,4′-bis(2-octyldodecyl)-2,2′-bithiophene (Scheme 24).302 The effect of the presence of electron deficient benzothiadiazole units in the polymer chain is manifested by an increase of the IP value to 5.18 eV i.e. by nearly 0.2 eV as compared to the case of P3HT studied under the same conditions.
